D) The role of matter

Key Takeaway
The second objection is answered by showing that the observable interaction is not in dispute; what matters is identifying the true agent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, when you witness changes—a recovery from illness, a conflict resolved, a door opening—do your thoughts immediately go to the apparent cause (a doctor, a peacemaker, a job opportunity) or to the True Agent behind it? What would it take for you to habitually see Allah’s hand first?
?
This lesson shows that the real dispute is about the agent, not the observable interactions. Are there areas in your heart where you have been treating people, systems, or your own efforts as independent agents, effectively forgetting that Allah alone is the Creator of every effect? How can you actively shift your reliance from those means to the True Agent today?
?
If the 'breaker' of qualities can be a form acting through accidental qualities, then even the things we rely on are merely channels. What are you most afraid of losing? Is it possible that your fear reveals that you have placed your trust in the channel rather than the Source? Will you ask Allah to make your heart depend only on Him?

Preferred Explanation: Forms Acting Through Qualities
Al-Taftazani gives his preferred view on how forms break intensities via qualities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's preferred explanation that the form acts through qualities (intrinsic or accidental, active or passive) to break opposing intensities, and the final clarification that matter is the true patient.

Core Idea
Forms act through qualities; matter is the real subject of change.

Having refuted earlier objections, the author now presents his own account: the water form, via accidental heat or intrinsic coldness, breaks the intensity of the opposite quality. He also clarifies that the real subject of change is matter, not the qualities themselves.

Guided Path
1
Read the preferred explanation
The author states that the breaker of the coldness intensity is the water form via accidental heat.
This avoids the need for a simple form as breaker.
2
Understand the rule of forms
The rule: each element's form acts in its own matter essentially and in its neighbor via a quality (intrinsic or accidental, active or passive).
This explains how forms interact without direct action on qualities.
3
Grasp the final clarification
The author addresses a final objection: that the passive object is the qualities themselves. He replies that qualities perish, but the true patient is matter, which can be affected by forms via passive qualities like moisture/dryness.
Example: water form breaks dryness of fire by its moisture, not coldness.

الصورة تجوز والحقيقة أن الصور والكيفيات معدات لفيضان الكيفية المتوسطة من المبدأ المفارق بطريق اللزوم (2) عند الفلاسفة لتمام الفاعل والقابل وبطريق العادة عند غيرهم لكون الفاعل مختاراً، وحينئذ يبطل حديث وإنما النزاع في الفاعل، وإن زعموا أن الكاسر لسورة برودة الماء الصورة النارية التي أحدثت الحرارة في الماء الحار. هو قلنا : فقد ظهر أنه ليس بلازم أن يكون الكاسر للكيفية صورة بسيط هو أحد أجزاء المركب. فبطل قولكم في المزاج ، بأن انكسار الكيفيات، إنما هو بصور عناصر الممتزج ، ثم الأشبه أن يقال: الكاسر السورة برودة الماء البارد المختلط ، أن بالماء الحار هو الصورة المائية بتوسط الحرارة العارضة. لأن من Commentary
This passage is a sequence of objections and answers concerning the interaction of qualities in mixture (imtizāj). The author, al-Taftazani, is discussing whether the agent (fāʿil) in the production of an intermediate quality (kayfiyya mutawassiṭa) is the form (ṣūra) or the quality itself, and whether forms are needed as breakers of opposing qualities.

First, an objection is raised: if qualities interact directly, then the breaking quality would have to be present at the same time as the broken quality, leading to a conjunction of contradictory intensities. The author gives two replies. The first reply is that the claim that forms are agents is a metaphor; in reality, forms and qualities are instruments for the emanation of the intermediate quality from the separate principle (al-mabdaʾ al-mufāriq). For philosophers, this is by way of concomitance (luzūm) when agent and recipient are complete; for others (theologians), it is by way of habit (ʿāda) because the agent is free. Thus the talk of dominance and being dominated becomes irrelevant. The second reply is that in mixture, what is broken is the intensity (sūra) of a quality, not the quality itself, while the breaker is the opposite quality itself, not its intensity. He gives the example of very hot water being broken by cold water, lukewarm water, or even less hot water. Hence the broken quality can break the intensity of the opposite quality without contradiction.

Then another objection is presented: we observe the occurrence of an intermediate quality by mere interaction of qualities, like hot and cold water mixing, without any form breaking the coldness. The opponent might claim that there is no acting and being acted upon (breaking and being broken) at all; rather, the matter becomes prepared by the conjunction of the two waters for the removal of their qualities and the emanation of an intermediate quality from the Emanating Principle (al-mabdaʾ al-fayyāḍ). The author replies: then let the same be said for mixture (mizāj) as well—intensification and weakening are nothing but the nullification of one quality and occurrence of another according to preparedness, and the dispute is only about the agent. If they claim the breaker is the fire form that caused heat, the author responds that it is not necessary that the breaker be a simple form that is part of the compound; rather, it could be the water form via the accidental heat. He then explains the rule: the form of each element acts essentially in its own matter, and in its neighbor by means of a quality (intrinsic or accidental, active or passive). The matter is affected essentially by its form and by neighboring qualities. This avoids the problems faced by those who say the agent is the quality: if breaking is between two active qualities (heat and cold), there would be affection of the active quality; if between two passive qualities (moisture and dryness), the passive quality would need to be active. The author's account avoids these.

Finally, a last objection: there is no doubt that the passive object in mixture is the qualities themselves. The author concedes that qualities perish and the intermediate quality occurs, but the true patient (that which is affected and changes) is matter alone. Just as matter can be affected in active qualities, it can be affected by the form acting through passive qualities, e.g., the water form breaks the dryness of fire by its moisture, not by its coldness.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the form directly breaks the intensity without involving any quality.
Correction: The form acts through a quality (intrinsic or accidental, active or passive).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson argues that when water and fire mix, the water form breaks the dryness of fire by its moisture, not by its coldness. Where in your life are you focusing on superficial qualities (like temperature or mood) rather than the deeper form or essence of a situation? Will you commit today to looking beyond the obvious 'qualities' to the underlying reality?
?
Al-Taftazani insists that matter alone is the true subject of change, while qualities come and go. Think of a recent time you were confused by changing emotions or circumstances. How often do you mistake these passing qualities for your unchanging core? What would it mean to identify with the 'matter' that endures rather than the qualities that perish?
?
The author says that the form acts through qualities to bring about change. Is there a quality in your character—like patience or honesty—that you have treated as the 'agent' itself? Consider that these qualities are merely instruments of a deeper self or spirit. Will you realign your focus onto the form (your soul or intention) rather than the mere quality?

Causality and Created Things

The True Agent in Breaking Qualities: Form, Not Quality
Sanusi refutes that the breaker is a simple form and explains the true agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi argues that the agent that breaks qualities in mixture is the substantial form acting through an accidental quality, not the quality itself.

Core Idea
The form acts through accidental qualities; the matter is the true subject of change.

The debate over mixture among theologians often centers on what actually breaks the qualities of the original elements. Some argue that a simple form (like the form of fire) directly breaks the coldness of water. Sanusi refutes this, proposing instead that the substantial form acts through an accidental quality acquired from the mixing. In this passage, he carefully distinguishes the roles of form, quality, and matter, and addresses a potential objection about the passivity of active qualities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Pay attention to the objection-and-answer structure.
2
Identify the two competing views
Notice the claim that the breaker is a simple form (e.g., fiery form breaking water's coldness) and Sanusi's alternative: the water form breaking coldness via accidental heat.
3
Understand the rules of elemental interaction
Examine the rules Sanusi cites: each element's form acts on its own matter essentially, and on its neighbor through a quality (essential or accidental, active or passive).
These rules are key to answering the objection.
4
See how the passivity objection is resolved
The objection claims that if the agent is the quality, problems arise (active quality becoming passive). Sanusi shows that if the agent is the form acting through a quality, these contradictions disappear.
Focus on the example of water's wetness breaking fire's dryness.
5
Note the final clarification about matter
Sanusi concludes that the qualities vanish, but the true subject of change is the matter, not the qualities themselves.
This corrects a common misunderstanding.

قلنا: فليكن الأمر في المزاج أيضاً كذلك. فإنه لا معنى لاشتداد الكيفية وضعفها إلا بطلان كيفية وحدوث أخرى أشد منها أو أضعف بحسب اختلاف الاستعداد، وإنما النزاع في الفاعل، وإن زعموا أن الكاسر لسورة برودة الماء الصورة النارية التي أحدثت الحرارة في الماء الحار. هو قلنا: فقد ظهر أنه ليس بلازم أن يكون الكاسر للكيفية صورة بسيط هو أحد أجزاء المركب. فبطل قولكم في المزاج بأن انكسار الكيفيات إنما هو بصور عناصر الممتزج، ثم الأشبه أن يقال: الكاسر لسورة برودة الماء البارد المختلط بالماء الحار هو الصورة المائية بتوسط الحرارة العارضة. لأن من قواعدهم صورة كل عنصر تفعل في مادته بالذات، وفي مجاوره بواسطة الكيفية ذاتية كانت كبرودة الماء أو عرضية كحرارته فعلية كالحرارة والبرودة أو انفعالية كالرطوبة واليبوسة، ومادة كل عنصر تنفعل بالذات عن صورته وتتكيف بالكيفية الذاتية أو العرضية الفعلية والانفعالية عن مجاورة. وعلى هذا لا يرد على القائلين بأن الفاعل هو الصورة ما يرد على القائلين بكونه هو الكيفية من لزوم انفعال الكيفية الفعلية فيما إذا كان الكسر والانكسار بين الفعليتين أعني الحرارة والبرودة، ولزوم فعلية الكيفية الانفعالية فيما إذا كان الكسر والانكسار بين الانفعاليين أعني الرطوبة واليبوسة. فإن قيل: إن كان في الفاعلية خفاء فلا خفاء في أن المنفعل عند الامتزاج هو الكيفيات كحرارة النار وبرودة الماء وكذا البواقي. قلنا: نعم بمعنى أنها تزول وتحدث الكيفية المتوسطة، وأما الذي يتأثر ويتغير من حال إلى حال فهو المادة لا غير. وكما لا يمتنع انفعالها في الكيفية الفعلية كالحرارة والبرودة لا يمتنع فعل الصورة بالكيفية الانفعالية كالرطوبة واليبوسة، للقطع بأن صورة الماء مثلاً إنما تكسر يبوسة النار برطوبته لا ببرودته، وصورة النار تكسر رطوبة الماء بيبوستها لا بحرارتها.
We said: So let the matter be likewise in the mixture. For there is no meaning to the intensification and weakening of a quality except the annihilation of a quality and the occurrence of another stronger or weaker according to the difference of preparedness, and the dispute is only concerning the agent, even if they claim that the breaker of the form of the water's coldness is the fiery form which produced heat in the hot water. It is we said: So it has become apparent that it is not necessary that the breaker of the quality be a simple form which is one of the parts of the compound. Therefore your statement regarding mixture has been invalidated that the breaking of qualities is only by the forms of the elements of the mixture. Then the more appropriate is to say: The breaker of the form of the coldness of the cold water mixed with the hot water is the water form through the mediation of the accidental heat. For it is among their rules: the form of each element acts upon its matter essentially, and upon its neighbor by means of a quality, whether essential like the coldness of water, or accidental like its heat, active like heat and cold, or passive like moisture and dryness. And the matter of each element is acted upon essentially by its form and is qualified by the essential or accidental active or passive quality from the neighbor. And on this, what one objects to those who say that the agent is the form does not apply to those who say that it is the quality: the necessity of the passivity of the active quality when the breaking occurs between the two active ones, i.e., heat and cold, and the necessity of the activity of the passive quality when the breaking occurs between the two passive ones, i.e., moisture and dryness. For if it is said: If there is obscurity concerning the agency, there is no obscurity that that which is acted upon during mixture is the qualities, like the heat of fire and the coldness of water, and likewise the rest. We said: Yes, in the sense that they vanish and the intermediate quality occurs. But that which is affected and changes from one state to another is the matter alone. And just as its passivity is not impossible in the active quality like heat and cold, so the form's acting by the passive quality like moisture and dryness is not impossible, for it is certain that the form of water, for example, only breaks the dryness of fire by its wetness, not by its coldness, and the form of fire breaks the wetness of water by its dryness, not by its heat.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and objection-answer in a kalam discussion on mixture (imtizaj). The author begins by stating that the intensification and weakening of a quality simply means one quality is annihilated and another arises, determined by preparedness. The real dispute is about the agent: what breaks the original quality? Some say it is a simple form (the substantial form of one element) that breaks the quality of another. The author refutes this by first stating that it is not necessary that the breaker be a simple form; rather, the more plausible view is that the water form (the substantial form of water) breaks the coldness of the cold water through the medium of accidental heat (the heat that the water acquired when mixed with hot water). He then explains the rules underlying this: each elemental form acts on its own matter essentially and on its neighbor through a quality—either essential (like water's coldness) or accidental (like heat), and that quality can be active (heat/cold) or passive (moisture/dryness). The matter of each element is acted upon essentially by its own form and becomes qualified by the neighbor's quality. On this basis, the objection that raises contradictions for those who say the agent is the quality (i.e., the active quality itself) does not apply to those who say the agent is the form. Specifically, if the agent were the active quality, then when two active qualities (heat and cold) interact, the active quality would itself be passive, which is problematic; similarly, if an active quality were to act on a passive one, the passive would become active. But if the agent is the form, these problems do not arise because the form acts through an accidental quality. Then an objection is raised: even if the agent is obscure, it is clear that the passive subject in mixture is the qualities themselves (e.g., heat and cold are annihilated). The author answers: yes, the qualities vanish and an intermediate quality arises, but the thing that actually undergoes change from one state to another is the matter, not the qualities themselves. Just as matter can be passive to active qualities, it can also be the locus for the form's action through passive qualities. For example, water's form breaks fire's dryness by its own essential wetness, not by its coldness; fire's form breaks water's wetness by its own dryness, not by its heat.

انفعال
استعداد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The qualities themselves are the things that are affected and change during mixture.
Correction: The qualities vanish and an intermediate quality occurs, but the actual subject that is affected and changes from one state to another is the matter alone.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the actual subject that is affected and changes from one state to another during mixture?
A) The qualities themselves
B) The form of the element
C) The matter
D) The intermediate quality

Key Takeaway
The agent that breaks qualities in mixture is the substantial form acting through an accidental quality, and the matter is the real patient of change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think about a time you underwent a deep personal change. Was it merely an external 'quality' (a habit or action) that changed, or was it your inner 'form' (your essential character) that shifted? How does this lesson’s distinction between agent and patient help you understand the true source of lasting transformation in your life? What will you do to ensure your change is from your core?
?
The author argues that the patient of change is matter, not the qualities. In your spiritual journey, what is the 'matter' of your soul that must be reshaped? Are you too focused on acquiring and discarding superficial 'qualities' (e.g., performing rituals without reflection) while neglecting the essence that Allah wants to transform? Ask yourself honestly: what is the one deep-rooted trait you have been avoiding changing?
?
If the form acts through accidental qualities, then sometimes God uses unexpected means to break your harmful 'qualities' (like pride or indifference). Has there been a situation where a trial came through a seemingly unrelated channel (like a kind word from a stranger) that broke a negative pattern in you? How can you become more attentive to these subtle agents of change in your daily life, recognizing that their source is ultimately from Allah?

Definition of Similar Mixture Quality and Its Necessity
Sanusi defines the similarity of mixture quality and its conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the similarity of mixture quality and why it requires a real uniform quality across all parts, not just perceptual similarity.

Core Idea
True mixture requires a real uniform quality in every part, not just appearance.

This passage from Sanusi clarifies one of the key concepts in natural philosophy: what it means for a mixture to have a similar quality throughout. He distinguishes true mixture from mere composition and explains why a genuine intermediate quality is necessary for the mixture to receive new forms.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once to get an overview of the definition and its implications.
Focus on the meaning of 'similarity' in this context.
2
Identify the definition
Find the sentence that defines the similarity of mixture quality. Note that it requires equality in specific reality across parts, differing only in location.
The fiery part is said to share heat, cold, etc., with the watery part.
3
Understand the consequence of lacking real similarity
Why does the author argue that mere perceptual similarity is insufficient? Because without a real intermediate quality, there is no action/passion and no preparation for new forms.
This connects to the philosophical principle that mixture must produce a new quality.
4
Distinguish mixture from composition
Note the author's distinction: mixture involves a new intermediate quality; composition is more general and may lack this. Check the examples and the reference to al-Shifa.
Also note that some scholars use 'ikhtilat' synonymously with 'imtizaj'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع: أن معنى تشابه الكيفية المزاجية في الكل أن الحاصل في كل جزء من الأجزاء المركبة أو البسيطة للممتزج تماثل الحاصل في الجزء الآخر أي تساويه في الحقيقة النوعية من غير تفاوت إلا بالمحل، حتى أن الجزء الناري كالجزء المائي في الحرارة والبرودة والرطوبة واليبوسة وكذا الهوائي والأرضي، إذ لو اختلفت الكيفيات في أجزاء الممتزج وكان التشابه في الحس لشدة امتزاج الكيفيات العنصرية الباقية على حالها بحيث لا تتميز عند الحس لما كان هناك فعل وانفعال لم تتحقق كيفية وجودانية بها يستعد الممتزج لفيضان صورة معدنية أو نباتية أو حيوانية أو نفس إنسانية عليه بل كان هذا مجرد تركيب ومجاورة بين العناصر لا امتزاج لأن الامتزاج هو اجتماع العناصر بحيث تحدث منه الكيفية المتوسطة المتشابهة، والتركيب أعم من ذلك، وكذا الاختلاط وقد يجعل مرادفاً للامتزاج كذا في الشفاء، وما ذكر في شرح القانون من أن معنى التشابه في جميع الأجزاء أن يستحر بالقياس إلى البارد ويستبرد بالقياس إلى الحار وكذا في الرطوبة واليبوسة قصداً إلى دفع اعتراض الإمام بدخول توابع المزاج في تعريفه فمخالفة لصريح العقل وصحيح النقل، وما ذكرنا هو المفهوم من اللفظ والمذكور في كلام القوم. قال: فلا بد من استحالة العناصر في كيفياتها جميعاً. قد عرفت فيما مضى أن الكون والفساد تبدل في الصورة النوعية للعناصر.
The fourth: That the meaning of the similarity of the mixture quality in the whole is that what obtains in each part of the composite or simple parts of the mixture is similar to what obtains in the other part, i.e., it equals it in specific reality without difference except in location, such that the fiery part is like the watery part in heat, cold, moisture, and dryness, and likewise the airy and earthy. For if the qualities differed in the parts of the mixture and the similarity were perceptual due to the intensity of the mixing of the elemental qualities remaining in their state such that they are not distinguished by sense, then there would be no action and passion, and an existential quality would not be realized by which the mixture becomes prepared for the influx of a mineral, plant, animal, or human soul form. Rather, this would be mere composition and adjacency between the elements, not mixture, because mixture is the joining of elements such that the intermediate similar quality arises from it, and composition is more general than that, and likewise mixing, and it may be made synonymous with mixture, as in al-Shifa. And what was mentioned in Sharh al-Qanun, that the meaning of similarity in all parts is that it is hot relative to the cold and cold relative to the hot, and likewise for moisture and dryness, aiming to repel the Imam's objection regarding the inclusion of concomitant accidents of mixture in its definition, is contrary to clear reason and sound transmission. And what we have mentioned is the meaning understood from the expression and mentioned in the speech of the authorities. He said: So there must be transformation of the elements in all their qualities. You have already known earlier that generation and corruption are a change in the specific form of the elements.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage contains the fourth point in a classification of issues related to mixture. It defines what is meant by the similarity of the mixture quality (al-kayfiyya al-mizajiyya) across all parts. The definition: the quality present in every part of the mixture (whether composite or simple) is similar in specific reality to the quality in every other part, with no difference except in the particular substance (location). For example, the fiery part shares the same heat, cold, moisture, and dryness as the watery part. The author then explains the consequence if qualities were merely perceptually similar due to fine mixing while remaining unchanged: there would be no real action and passion, and no genuine intermediate quality would arise. Without such a quality, the mixture could not receive a new mineral, plant, animal, or human soul form—it would be mere juxtaposition (tarkib) and adjacency (mujawara), not true mixture (imtizaj). The author distinguishes mixture from composition and mixing (ikhtilat), though some make them synonymous. He then criticizes a definition given in Sharh al-Qanun, which defined similarity relative to hot/cold and moist/dry, as contrary to reason and transmitted knowledge. Finally, he quotes the original text (matn): 'So there must be transformation of the elements in all their qualities.' The commentator then reminds that generation and corruption (kawn wa fasad) involve a change in the specific form of the elements.

Key Terms
كيفية مزاجية
تشابه
امتزاج
تركيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that perceptual similarity due to fine mixing is sufficient for a true mixture.
Correction: The author argues that without a real uniform quality, there is no genuine mixture; the elements must produce a new intermediate quality.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what distinguishes true mixture (imtizaj) from mere composition (tarkib)?
A) In mixture, the elements remain unchanged
B) In mixture, a new intermediate similar quality arises from the combination
C) In composition, the elements lose their identities
D) There is no difference; the terms are synonymous

Key Takeaway
True mixture requires a real uniform quality in every part arising from the interaction of elements, not just perceptual similarity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In this lesson, you learned that mere perceptual similarity without a real inner change is insufficient for true mixture. Consider your own spiritual life: are you content with a 'perceptual' faith—practices that look good to others—while your inner qualities remain unchanged? What specific area of your character might still retain its 'original elemental selfishness' rather than being transformed into a new, uniform sincerity in seeking Allah?
?
The passage warns that without a genuine existential quality, the mixture cannot receive a higher form (like a human soul). Reflect: if your soul is meant to be a mixture of body and spirit prepared to receive divine grace, what 'perceptual similarities' (e.g., outward piety) might be masking the absence of real transformation? What one action will you take today to move from 'composition' —a list of good deeds—to 'mixture'—where every part of your life is uniformly animated by the remembrance of Allah?

Critique of Alternative Definitions and Necessity of Elemental Transformation
Sanusi criticizes an alternative definition and concludes that elements must transform.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the criticism of an alternative definition of mixture similarity and the conclusion that elements must transform in all their qualities for true mixture.

Core Idea
Elements must truly transform in all qualities for mixture; perceptual relativity is insufficient.

After defining his position, Sanusi addresses a competing definition from Sharh al-Qanun that defined similarity in relative terms. He refutes it as contrary to reason and transmitted knowledge, and then asserts the necessity of elemental transformation, linking it to the concept of generation and corruption.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the alternative definition and the author's response.
Pay attention to the specific wording of the alternative and the rejection.
2
Understand the alternative definition
The definition from Sharh al-Qanun says similarity means the mixture is hot relative to cold and cold relative to hot, and similarly for moisture/dryness. This was an attempt to avoid an objection by Avicenna.
The motivation was to exclude accidental concomitants of mixture from the definition.
3
See why the author rejects it
Sanusi says this definition contradicts clear reason (sarih al-'aql) and sound transmission (sahih al-naql). He implies it fails to capture the real transformation required.
He then reaffirms his own definition as the one understood from the language and the authorities.
4
Grasp the necessity of transformation
The original text (matn) states: 'So there must be transformation of the elements in all their qualities.' The commentator explains that generation and corruption involve change in the specific form of the elements.
This ties the discussion to broader cosmological principles.

Source Text

The fourth: That the meaning of the similarity of the mixture quality in the whole is that what obtains in each part of the composite or simple parts of the mixture is similar to what obtains in the other part, i.e., it equals it in specific reality without difference except in location, such that the fiery part is like the watery part in heat, cold, moisture, and dryness, and likewise the airy and earthy. ?
If the elements must undergo a total re-creation for a true mixture, what in your life needs to be fully undone and remade—not just adjusted around the edges—starting today? What step will you take right now to begin that transformation?

Definition and Proof of Istihalah with Objection
Defines istihalah, gives two proofs, and presents an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of istihalah, its distinction from kawn wa fasad, the two proofs for its existence, and the key objection raised against the second proof.

Core Idea
Istihalah is change of qualities while the form remains; it is the basis of mizaj and is proven by the necessity of gradual change.

This passage from the Sharh al-Maqasid clarifies the contested concept of istihalah (transmutation). After defining it precisely, the author presents two arguments for its reality and then considers a powerful objection. Understanding this discussion is crucial for grasping how composite substances (such as living bodies) arise from elemental mixture.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Start by reading the opening sentences where istihalah is defined as a change in qualities while the form (substance) remains. Note how it differs from kawn wa fasad (generation and corruption).
The author clearly states: 'we mean by istihalah only the change of quality with the persistence of the form.'
2
Follow the first proof from kawn wa fasad
The passage refutes an objection by linking istihalah to the general principle of generation and corruption: since forms change gradually, the qualities must change first. Trace this argument step by step.
This proof relies on the idea that material change requires time, so it cannot be instantaneous in the form.
3
Examine the second proof from emanation
The second proof argues that because forms and souls emanate from above, matter must first acquire an intermediate quality (istihalah) to receive them. Read this section and notice how it connects istihalah to the broader metaphysical framework.
This is presented as an alternative proof from the matn.
4
Consider the objection to the second proof
The passage ends with an objection: the intermediate quality could result from mere mechanical mixture without actual transmutation of each part's innate quality. Note that the response is not given here; this leaves room for further discussion.
The objection challenges the necessity of istihalah in the second sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بأن تبطل صورة، وتحدث أخرى مع بقاء المادة والاستحالة تبدل في الكيفيات، بأن تزول كيفية، وتحدث أخرى مع بقاء الصورة ولا خفاء في أن القول بالمزاج بالمعنى المذكور. أعني حدوث كيفية متوسطة متشابهة في كل جزء بحسب الحقيقة، مبنى على جواز استحالة كل عنصر في كيفية الفعلية والانفعالية، حتى يكون الجزء الناري من الممتزج في الكيفية المتوسطة بين الحرارة والبرودة، والرطوبة واليبوسة كالجزء المائي، والهوائي والأرضي على السواء. وزعم الإمام أنهم لم يثبتوا ذلك إلا في الماء حيث يستحيل برده إلى الحر من غير تكون وبروز، ولا ورود عليه من خارج، وهو لا يستلزم جواز استحالة الكل في الكل وكأن الأطباء تركوا بيان هذا الأصل إلى الحكماء، لكونه من مبادىء علم الطب، والحكماء إلى الأطباء لكونه من فروع الطبيعي، وأصول الطب فبقي مهملاً. ورد بأن جواز الاستحالة من لوازم جواز الكون والفساد، فبيانه في الكل بيان لجواز الاستحالة في الكل، وتقريره على ما أشير إليه في النجاة، أن زوال صورة وحدوث أخرى إنما يكون عند تمام استعداد المادة وهو أمر حادث يفتقر إلى زمان، فلا بد من تغير واقع على التدريج، وليس ذلك في نفس الصورة لأن وجودها وعدمها دفعي. فتعين أن يكون في الكيفية بأن تتغير فتضعف الكيفية التي تناسب الصورة التي تفسد وتشتد إلى تناسب الصورة التي تكون ولا نعني بالاستحالة إلا تغير الكيفية مع بقاء الصورة وما ذكر في المتن استدلال على ثبوت الاستحالة بوجه آخر، وهو أنه لما ثبت فيضان الصور والنفوس لزم حدوث كيفية متوسطة متشابهة في جميع أجزاء الممتزج، لتستعد المادة بذلك لقبولها، وهذا نفس الاستحالة. أعني زوال الكيفيات الصرفة في الأجزاء العنصرية وحصول الكيفية المتوسطة وفيه نظر لجواز أن يحصل الاستعداد بمجرد اختلاط الأجزاء المتصغرة بحيث تحصل الكيفية المتوسطة بحسب الحس مع كون كل من الأجزاء البسيطة على صرافة كيفيتها.
By that a form ceases, and another occurs with the matter remaining; and istihalah (transmutation) is a change in the qualities, by a quality ceasing, and another occurring with the form remaining. There is no hiddenness in that the statement about mizaj (temperament) in the mentioned sense – i.e., the occurrence of an intermediate quality similar in every part according to reality – is based on the permissibility of transmutation of every element in its active and passive quality, so that the fiery part of the mixture is in the intermediate quality between heat and cold, and humidity and dryness, like the watery, airy, and earthy parts equally. And the Imam claimed that they have not established that except in water, where its coldness transmutes to heat without composition, emergence, or external influx, and that does not entail the permissibility of total transmutation; it is as if the physicians left the elucidation of this principle to the philosophers, because it belongs to the principles of medicine, and the philosophers to the physicians, because it belongs to branches of physics and principles of medicine, so it remained neglected. And it was refuted that the permissibility of transmutation is a necessary consequence of the permissibility of generation and corruption (kawn wa fasad); so its explanation in the whole is an explanation of the permissibility of transmutation in the whole. Its elaboration according to what was indicated in al-Najat: that the cessation of a form and the occurrence of another is only at the completion of the matter's preparedness, which is an originated matter requiring time; so there must be a change occurring gradually, and that is not in the form itself because its existence and non-existence are instantaneous. So it is determined that it is in the quality, by it changing: the quality suitable for the form that corrupts weakens, and the quality suitable for the form that comes to be intensifies. And we mean by istihalah only the change of quality with the persistence of the form. And what was mentioned in the matn is a proof for the establishment of istihalah in another way: that since the emanation of forms and souls is established, the occurrence of an intermediate quality similar in all parts of the mixture is necessary, so that matter thereby becomes prepared to receive them, and this is exactly istihalah – i.e., the removal of pure qualities from the elemental parts and the acquisition of the intermediate quality. But it is open to objection: because it is possible that preparedness occurs merely by the mixing of minute parts such that the intermediate quality is obtained perceptually while each simple part remains in the purity of its quality.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of istihalah (transmutation) as a change in accidental qualities while the substance (form) remains, distinguishing it from kawn wa fasad (generation and corruption) where the form itself changes. It begins by stating that mizaj (temperament) – an intermediate quality arising from mixture – depends on the possibility of each element transmuting in its active and passive qualities. The author then reports that a certain Imam (likely Imam al-Razi or similar) objected that this transmutation is only observed in water heating up, not universally, and that physicians and philosophers neglected to explain it. This objection is refuted by arguing that the permissibility of transmutation in any part follows from the general principle of kawn wa fasad, which requires gradual change; since material change takes time, the alteration must occur in the qualities rather than instantaneously in the form. The passage then introduces a second proof from the matn (original text): because forms and souls emanate from above, matter must first acquire an intermediate quality (the very istihalah) to receive them. This second proof is critiqued through the objection that mere mechanical mixture of minute particles might produce an apparent intermediate quality without actual transmutation of each part's innate quality. The objection is stated without an explicit counter-response in this passage.

مزاج
كون وفساد
كيفية
صورة
مادة
استعداد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That istihalah is the same as kawn wa fasad (generation and corruption).
Correction: The passage explicitly defines istihalah as change in qualities with persistence of form, while kawn wa fasad involves change of form itself.

Checkpoint
What is the primary difference between istihalah and kawn wa fasad according to this passage?
A) Istihalah involves change of qualities with persistence of form, while kawn wa fasad involves change of form.
B) Istihalah occurs instantaneously, while kawn wa fasad is gradual.
C) Istihalah applies only to inanimate objects, kawn wa fasad to living things.
D) There is no difference; both terms are synonymous.

Key Takeaway
Istihalah is a real change in qualities that enables mixture and prepares matter to receive new forms; it is distinct from generation and corruption and is proven by the gradual nature of material change.

Objection and Answer on Elemental Forms Persisting
Sanusi presents an objection about the persistence of elemental forms and answers it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi defends the persistence of elemental forms in mixtures against the objection that it would cause a single part to have two forms.

Core Idea
The new form only affects compound parts, not simple elemental parts.

In this passage, Sanusi addresses a critical objection to the idea that elemental forms remain after mixing. The opponent argues that if elemental forms persist and the new form permeates everything, then each part would have two forms, leading to absurd consequences. Sanusi's answer clarifies the scope of the new form's influence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The opponent claims that if elemental forms persist and the new form permeates all parts, then a part like fire would have both its own form and the form of gold, implying generation from a single element.
2
Identify the answer
Sanusi responds by restricting the new form to compound parts only, not simple parts.
3
Reflect on the implication
This preserves elemental forms while avoiding the absurdity of a single element generating compounds.
Consider how this resolves the apparent contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : لو كانت صور العناصر باقية، والصورة الحادثة بعد المزاج سارية في جميع أجزاء الممتزج لزم أن تكون النار مثلاً مع الصورة النارية، متصفـة بالصورة الذهبية، وحينئذ جاز أن تكون المواليد من عنصر واحد . قلنا: يجوز أن تكون الصورة الحادثة إنما تسري في الأجزاء المركبة دون الأجزاء البسيطة.
For if it is said: If the forms of the elements persist, and the form that occurs after the temperament permeates all parts of the mixture, then it would follow that fire, for example, with its fiery form, is described with the golden form, and then it could be that generated things are from a single element. We say: It is possible that the occurring form only permeates the compound parts, not the simple parts.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objection argues: if the elemental forms (ṣuwar al-ʿanāṣir) remain after mixing, and the new form (e.g., the form of gold) permeates all parts of the mixture, then each elemental part (e.g., fire) would possess both its original form and the new form simultaneously. This would imply that a single element (like fire alone) could generate compound substances, which is absurd. The answer is: the new form (al-ṣūra al-ḥāditha) does not permeate the simple elemental parts (al-ajzāʾ al-basīṭa al-ʿunṣuriyya); it only permeates the compound parts (al-ajzāʾ al-murakkaba). Thus, the elemental forms remain in the simple parts, but the compound parts receive the new form, avoiding the absurdity.

Key Terms
صور العناصر
صورة حادثة
أجزاء مركبة
أجزاء بسيطة
مواليد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The new form must be present in every part of the mixture, including the simple elemental parts.
Correction: The author restricts the new form to compound parts only, not the simple parts.

Checkpoint
How does the author answer the objection that if elemental forms persist, then a single element could have two forms?
A) He denies that elemental forms persist
B) He says the new form only applies to compound parts, not the simple parts
C) He says the forms are not real
D) He says the objection is invalid because forms cannot coexist

Key Takeaway
The new form in a mixture only applies to compound parts, not the simple elemental parts, preserving the persistence of elemental forms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have core traits that feel unchanging—your nature, your fitrah. But you also have acquired traits shaped by experience. Where in your life have you resisted change because you feared losing your essence? How does Sanusi's distinction between simple and compound parts free you to embrace transformation without losing who you are at your core? Commit to one area where you will allow the compound parts of your character to be reshaped by divine guidance.
?
The objection assumes that if forms persist, then change is an illusion. Reflect: Have you ever dismissed personal growth as superficial, believing your deep flaws could never change? How does the answer—that change occurs in compound parts while simple parts remain—challenge you to take responsibility for the parts of you that can be transformed? Write down one specific habit you will intentionally reshape this week, trusting that your fundamental identity remains secure in Allah.

Defining the Relevant Type of Mixture
Defines which type of mixture is the subject of discussion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which type of mixture (al-mizaj) is the subject of kalam discussions and why mixtures arising from specific forms of compounds are excluded.

Core Idea
Not all mixtures are alike—kalam focuses only on those arising from elemental interactions.

This passage from the matn clarifies a crucial distinction. The author contrasts two theories of mixture: one where elemental qualities break while their forms remain, and another where a new specific form is infused. The latter is excluded from the definition. Let's read the passage carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Pay attention to the contrast between the two theories.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two theories
Find where the first theory (breaking of qualities) is described and where the second theory (specific forms) is described.
Look for the phrases 'انكسار الكيفيات' and 'الصور النوعية'.
3
Understand the exclusion
The author states that the second theory does not enter the definition. Why? Because the mixture must arise from the interaction of elemental powers, not from a superimposed specific form.
The gold example illustrates the second theory.
4
Reflect on significance
Consider why this distinction matters for kalam cosmology. The type of mixture under discussion is fundamental to understanding generation and corruption in the natural world.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحاصل من امتزاج الزئبق والكبريت، إن جعلناه حادثاً من انكسار الكيفيات بصور البسائط العنصرية المحفوظة في الممتزج على ما يظهر بالقرع والإنبيق، فإنا إذا وضعنا فيه قطعة من اللحم مثلاً تميزت إلى جسم مائي قاطر، وأرضى متكلس. وأما إذا جعلنا حدوثه بواسطة الصور النوعية للمركبات بأن تعد الكيفية المزاجية الأجزاء الممتزجة لفيضان صورة نوعية عليها غير صور العناصر، ثم تتفاعل الممتزجات المختلفة بواسطة صورها وكيفياتها، فتحدث كيفية متوسطة متشابهة في الشكل كما في الذهب بواسطة الصورة الزئبقية والكبريتية، فلا يدخل في التعريف، لأنها لم تحدث من تفاعل العناصر بقواها أي صورها أو كيفياتها.
The result from the mixture of mercury and sulfur: if we make it occurring by the breaking of the qualities through the forms of the elemental simples preserved in the mixture, as appears by distillation and the alembic, then if we place in it a piece of flesh, for example, it separates into a watery flowing body and a calcined earthy [body]. And if we make its occurrence by means of the specific forms of compounds, such that the temperamental quality prepares the mixed parts for the emanation of a specific form upon them different from the forms of the elements, then the different mixtures interact by means of their forms and qualities, and an intermediate quality similar in shape occurs, as in gold by means of the mercurial and sulfureous form, then it does not enter into the definition, because it did not occur from the interaction of the elements by their powers, i.e., their forms or qualities.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage defines the type of mixture (al-mizaj) under discussion by contrasting two theories. The first theory explains mixture as the breaking (inkisar) of elemental qualities while their forms remain, evidenced by distillation where a piece of flesh separates into water and earth. The second theory explains mixture through specific forms of compounds: a temperamental quality prepares the mixture for a new specific form, generating an intermediate quality like gold from mercury and sulfur. The author excludes the second from the definition because the desired mixture must result from the direct interaction of elemental powers (their forms or qualities), not from superimposed specific forms.

Key Terms
المزاج
الكيفية المتوسطة
الصور النوعية
انكسار الكيفيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All mixtures are the same and fall under the same definition in kalam.
Correction: The passage distinguishes mixtures arising from direct elemental interaction (accepted) from those arising from specific forms (excluded).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of mixture is excluded from the definition?
A) That which occurs by breaking of qualities
B) That which occurs by specific forms of compounds
C) That which occurs by interaction of elemental powers
D) That which occurs by both

Key Takeaway
The mixture relevant to kalam must result from the direct interaction of elemental powers, not from the infusion of specific forms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your spiritual life, do you find yourself performing acts of worship that are like the 'specific forms' – outward shape without inner transformation? Or are your deeds arising from the 'elemental powers' of your heart, broken and reshaped by faith? Which would you rather have, and what will you change today to move from external form to internal reality?
?
The passage distinguishes between mixtures that preserve their elements and those that seem uniform but have no real internal interaction. Consider your connections with others: are you simply mixing with people on the surface, or are you truly interacting and being transformed by their elemental qualities? Who in your life are you just 'mixed' with, and who are you truly combined with in a way that changes you?
?
Gold is a beautiful result, but the passage says it is not the relevant kind of mixture because it doesn't come from the direct interaction of elements. Think about something you are proud of in your life – is it a 'gold' from external forms, or does it come from the raw materials of your soul? Are you willing to let Allah break your qualities to produce a true mixture, even if it means losing the luster of apparent success?

The Nature of Mizaj: A Tangible Quality with Preserved Forms
Enumerates opinions on mizaj and affirms the Peripatetic view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Peripatetics define mizaj (mixture) as a tangible quality that preserves elemental forms while transforming their qualities into an intermediate quality, and distinguish their view from alternative positions.

Core Idea
In mizaj, elemental forms remain; only their qualities change to an intermediate.

In this passage, the author clarifies the nature of mizaj (mixture) as a distinct tangible quality. He begins by stating that mizaj occurs in every part of a mixed body, preserving the specific forms of the elements while altering their pure qualities. He then reports three alternative opinions before affirming the first as the position of the majority of Peripatetics. This discussion is foundational for understanding how mixtures work in natural philosophy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to get an overview. Note the different 'qila' statements.
The passage contains four distinct views on what happens to elemental forms and qualities during mixture.
2
Identify the four opinions
List the four views: (a) mizaj is a quality with forms preserved and qualities changed; (b) both forms and qualities remain; (c) forms pass away to an intermediate; (d) it is a new specific form.
These are presented in the text: 'He said...', 'And it was said...' three times.
3
Understand the majority view
Focus on the final paragraph where the author affirms the first opinion as the Peripatetic position. Notice that mizaj is a tangible quality different in kind from pure elemental qualities, present in every part, with forms unchanged.
The key phrase is 'هذا رأي جمهور المشائين' – this is the opinion of the majority of Peripatetics.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask why preserving forms matters for the Peripatetic theory of mixture. Connect to the broader concept of causality and change.
Preserving forms allows the elements to remain potentially present, which is important for explaining how mixtures can be reversed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال فالمزاج نوع آخر من الكيفيات الملموسة حاصلة في كل جزء حتى البسائط، وهي على صورها دون كيفياتها . وقيل وكيفياتها. وإنما تحس بالمتوسطة للامتزاج . وقيل : بل زالت صورها إلى صورة متوسطة بينها . وقيل : بل صورة أخرى من النوعيات. قد علم مما سبق أن المزاج كيفية ملموسة مغايرة بالنوع ، لما في العناصر من الكيفيات الصرفة حاصلة في كل جزء من أجزاء الممتزج حتى الأجزاء البسيطة العنصرية، وهي باقية على صورها النوعية وإنما استحالت من كيفياتها الصرفة، إلى الكيفية المتوسطة وهذا رأي جمهور المشائين.
He said: 'The mixture (al-mizaj) is another kind of tangible qualities, occurring in every part, even the simples, and they [the elements] remain in their forms without their qualities.' And it was said: 'And their qualities [remain] as well.' And it is only sensed as intermediate because of the mixture. And it was said: 'Rather their forms have passed away to an intermediate form between them.' And it was said: 'Rather [it is] another form from the specific forms.' It has been known from what preceded that the mixture is a tangible quality different in kind from the pure qualities in the elements, occurring in every part of the mixed thing, even the simple elemental parts, and they remain in their specific forms, but their pure qualities have changed to the intermediate quality. This is the opinion of the majority of the Peripatetics.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage presents the author's position on the nature of mixture (al-mizaj). He begins by citing a statement that mizaj is a tangible quality distinct from elemental qualities, present in every part including the simple ones, with elemental forms preserved but their qualities changed to an intermediate quality. He then reports alternative opinions: some say qualities also remain, others say forms pass away to an intermediate form, and others say a new specific form arises. The author then affirms the first opinion as the position of the majority of Peripatetics (jumhur al-masha'in): mizaj is a tangible quality different in kind from the pure elemental qualities, present in all parts, while the elemental forms remain and only their pure qualities transmute to the intermediate quality.

Key Terms
المزاج
الكيفية الملموسة
الكيفية المتوسطة
الصور النوعية
المشائون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: In mixture, elemental forms cease to exist.
Correction: The Peripatetic view states that elemental forms remain; only their pure qualities are transformed into an intermediate quality.

Checkpoint
What is the opinion of the majority of Peripatetics regarding mixture (al-mizaj)?
A) Elemental forms pass away to an intermediate form
B) Elemental forms remain and their qualities change to an intermediate quality
C) Elemental forms and qualities both remain unchanged
D) A new specific form entirely replaces elemental forms

Key Takeaway
Mizaj is a tangible quality in which elemental forms are preserved but their pure qualities transmute to an intermediate quality according to the Peripatetics.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

When you consider the changes in your own character over time, do you believe there is a core 'form' of who you are that remains constant, even as your qualities shift? How does the Peripatetic view on mizaj challenge or affirm your understanding of your own identity?

Objection on Remaining Elemental Forms and Its Answer
Presents an objection about elemental forms remaining and two possible answers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the kalam objection regarding the persistence of elemental forms after mixture and the two key responses that preserve the possibility of elemental coexistence.

Core Idea
A new form may not permeate all parts equally; partial or conditional acceptance resolves the objection.

This lesson tackles a core critique in kalam cosmology: if elemental forms remain after mixture, how can a new form also exist in the same substance? The objection seems to imply absurd consequences. Sanusi's answer reveals subtle metaphysical distinctions about how forms relate to parts and the conditions of mixture.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if the forms remained... then it would be necessary that...' This sets up the logical problem.
The objection uses the example of fire acquiring a golden form.
2
Identify the two answers
After 'We say:', there are two distinct responses. Identify each one: (1) the new form only permeates compound parts, not simple ones; (2) the acceptance by simple parts is conditional on mixture.
These are not mutually exclusive; either can block the absurd conclusion.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why the objection fails. The key is that the new form does not have to be present in every single part equally. This preserves the possibility of elemental diversity and generation from multiple elements.
The phrase 'other false doctrines' signals that the author rejects alternative views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : لو كانت صور العناصر باقية، والصورة الحادثة بعد المزاج سارية في جميع أجزاء الممتزج لزم أن تكون النار مثلاً مع الصورة النارية، متصفة بالصورة الذهبية، وحينئذ جاز أن تكون المواليد من عنصر واحد . قلنا: يجوز أن تكون الصورة الحادثة إنما تسري في الأجزاء المركبة دون البسيطة، أو يكون قبول البسيط إياها مشروطاً بالامتزاج . ثم ههنا مذاهب أخر فاسدة .
For if it is said: 'If the forms of the elements remained, and the form occurring after mixture permeates all parts of the mixed thing, then it would be necessary that fire, for example, with its fiery form be qualified by the golden form, and then it would be possible that generated things [come] from one element.' We say: 'It is possible that the occurring form only permeates the compound parts, not the simple ones, or that the acceptance of it by the simple [part] is conditioned by mixture.' Then here are other false doctrines.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objection argues: if elemental forms remain and the new form from mixture permeates all parts, then a single element like fire would simultaneously have its own form and the new form (e.g., golden), implying that all generated things could come from one element—an absurdity. The author answers with two possibilities: either the new form only affects compound parts while simple parts retain only the elemental form, or simple parts accept the new form only conditionally, i.e., when mixed. The phrase "other false doctrines" transitions to the next lesson.

Correction: The author shows that the new form can be limited to compound parts or accepted conditionally, preserving coexistence without contradiction.

The Illusion of Pure Qualities: First False Doctrine on Elements
Refutes the doctrine of pure qualities; mixture is only apparent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that elements do not retain their pure qualities upon contact, contrary to the claim that mixture only hides them.

Core Idea
Elements truly change upon contact; mixture is not mere illusion.

This lesson examines the first false doctrine regarding elemental qualities: that elements keep their pure forms and qualities, and what we perceive as intermediate qualities is just a result of extreme mixing beyond sensory discrimination. The refutation is definitive: it is certain knowledge that qualities do not remain unchanged when elements meet. Let's explore this key principle in Islamic natural theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the source passage carefully. Notice the structure: the false doctrine is presented first, then its refutation.
2
Understand the false doctrine
The doctrine claims elements remain pure in form and quality; the perceived intermediate quality is due to extreme mixing and lack of sensory discrimination.
This is an illusion-based view of mixture.
3
Examine the refutation
The refutation states that it is known with certainty (maluum qat'an) that elements do not remain on their qualities when they contact each other. This is based on empirical observation.
No need for philosophical argument; it's a matter of clear certainty.
4
Reflect on the significance
This establishes that when elements mix, their qualities undergo real change, not just apparent mixing. It has implications for understanding physical change.
This foundational principle is used later for arguments about bodies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The first: that the elements remain in their forms and the purity of their qualities, and the intermediate quality is only sensed due to extreme mixing and lack of distinction to the senses. It was refuted by [saying] that the non-remaining of the elements upon their qualities when they contact is known with certainty.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage presents the first false doctrine (madhhab fasid) and its refutation. The doctrine holds that elements retain both their forms and pure qualities, and what appears as an intermediate quality is merely an illusion caused by extreme mixing beyond sensory discrimination. The refutation is decisive: it is known with certainty that elemental qualities do not remain unchanged when elements contact each other—a fact established by empirical observation (e.g., fire changes water).

Second False Doctrine and Its Refutations
Refutes the doctrine that elemental forms are replaced by a single new form

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second false doctrine about elemental forms being replaced by a single new form and the two rational and empirical refutations against it.

Core Idea
A single form for all elements contradicts observable chemical differences.

This passage presents a second false doctrine about mixture: that the elemental forms are completely replaced by a single new form, resulting in one matter and one form. Sanusi refutes this doctrine using both logical reasoning and empirical evidence. As you read, notice how he first explains the doctrine's variants, then offers two distinct refutations.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic once without analyzing, then read the translation. Let the author's own argument come through.
2
Identify the doctrine and its variants
The doctrine claims elements shed their forms and take on a single form. Two variants are mentioned: an intermediate form between contraries, or a new specific form for some types.
Notice that the doctrine is not monolithic; there are different interpretations.
3
Study the two refutations
The first refutation is logical: the corruption of forms (by breaking or removal) cannot happen simultaneously or successively, and the cause cannot be the quality because that would destroy effects. The second refutation is empirical: if there were only one form, mixtures would not behave differently in evaporation, distillation, calcination, but they do.
The first refutation relies on earlier arguments about qualities; the second uses observable chemical processes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : إن امتزاج العناصر وتفاعلها قد أدى بها إلى أن نخلع صورها، ولا يكون لواحد منها صورتها الخاصة، وتلبس حينئذ صورة واحدة، فيصير لها هيولي واحدة، وصورة واحدة، ثم منهم من جعل تلك الصورة أمراً متوسطاً بين الصور المتضادة للبسائط، ومنهم من جعلها صورة أخرى للنوعيات، أي صورة توجد لبعض الأنواع الموجودة في الأعيان . ورد بوجهين : أحدهما أن تفاسد الصور سواء كان على وجه الانكسار أو الزوال بالكلية، إما أن يكون معاً أو على التعاقب وكلاهما فاسد لما مرّ في الكيفيات، ولا يجوز أن يجعل الفاعل ههنا هو الكيفية كالصورة في انكسار الكيفيات، لأن في فساد الصورة فساد آثارها أعني الكيفيات. وثانيهما أنه لو كان كذلك لما اختلفت أجزاء الممتزج بالتبخر والتقاطر والترمد واللازم باطل بحكم القرع والإنبيق.
The second: that the mixture and interaction of the elements led them to shed their forms, and none of them has its own form, and then they put on a single form, so they come to have a single matter (hayula) and a single form. Then among them are those who make that form an intermediate thing between the contrary forms of the simples, and among them are those who make it another form from the specific forms, i.e., a form existing for some of the types existing in individuals. It was refuted in two ways: First, that the corruption (tafasud) of the forms, whether by breaking or complete removal, either occurs simultaneously or successively, and both are invalid as passed in the [discussion of] qualities. And it is not permissible to make the agent here the quality like the form in the breaking of qualities, because in the corruption of the form is the corruption of its effects, i.e., the qualities. Second, that if it were so, then the parts of the mixture would not differ in evaporation, distillation, and calcination, but the necessary consequence is false by the judgment of distillation and the alembic.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage presents the second false doctrine and its two refutations. The doctrine claims that elemental forms are completely replaced by a single new form, resulting in one matter and one form for the mixture. Some sub-variants consider this new form intermediate between elemental forms, others a completely new specific form. The first refutation argues that the corruption of forms (whether by breaking or total removal) cannot happen simultaneously or successively due to earlier arguments about qualities, and the cause (the quality) cannot act like a form because destroying the form destroys its effects (qualities). The second refutation appeals to empirical evidence: if there were only one form, the mixture's parts would not behave differently in processes like evaporation, distillation, and calcination, but experimentation (distillation and alembic) shows they do differ, proving multiple forms remain.

خلع الصور
هيولي واحدة
تفاسد الصور
التبخر
التقاطر
الترمد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think a single form is simpler and therefore preferable.
Correction: The refutation shows that a single form contradicts observable differentiation in chemical processes, so simplicity does not hold.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is one of the two refutations against the second false doctrine?
A) The forms must be eternal
B) The corruption of forms would lead to loss of their effects, and it cannot occur as described
C) The mixture would become a single element
D) The forms are not real

Key Takeaway
The doctrine of a single elemental form is refuted by both logical impossibility and empirical chemical differentiation.

Equilibrium in Mizaj: Definition and Impossibility Claim
Defines equilibrium in mixture and notes a claim of its impossibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of a balanced mixture (mizaj mu'tadil) and the rational argument that such equilibrium may be impossible.

Core Idea
A balanced mixture requires perfectly equal powers, but some argue it can never occur.

In this short passage, the author concludes the discussion of mixture (mizaj) by defining what makes it balanced: equality of the constituent powers. But he also notes a skeptical claim: such perfect balance may be impossible because nature only brings powers together through dominance. This lesson examines both the definition and the challenge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the literal meaning.
Notice the structure: first a definition, then a skeptical claim.
2
Understand the definition
Identify what makes a mixture 'balanced' according to the text: equality of powers in measure.
3
Examine the impossibility claim
Consider the reasoning: without a coercer, the only cause for combination is dominance of one power, which prevents equality.
Think about why this challenges the possibility of a truly balanced mixture.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: does this claim mean equilibrium is impossible in practice, or only in theory? The passage leaves it as a claim, not a conclusion.
This connects to broader discussions in Islamic theology about natural causation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال (ثم المزاج) إن كان من قوى متساوية المقادير فمعتدل، وقد يدعي امتناعه بناء على أن لا قاسر على الاجتماع سوى غلبة إحدى القوى.
He said: 'Then the mixture: if it is from powers equal in measure, then it is balanced (mu'tadil). And it may be claimed that it is impossible, based on the fact that there is no coercer for the coming together except the dominance of one of the powers.'
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion by defining equilibrium (i'tidal) in mixture: when the constituent powers are equal in magnitude, the resulting mizaj is balanced. It then notes a theoretical objection: some claim such equilibrium is impossible because there is no external coercer (qasir) to force the powers to come together without one dominating; in nature, mixture occurs only when one power overcomes another, leading to imbalance. The passage thus presents both the definition and a skeptical claim about its actual existence.

Two False Doctrines on Mixture Refuted
Author refutes two false theories on elemental mixture.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two false doctrines regarding elemental mixture and the rational and empirical arguments used to refute them.

Core Idea
Elements neither persist nor vanish in mixture—they transform genuinely.

In classical natural philosophy, the question of how elements combine to form compounds was hotly debated. Two extreme positions emerged: one claiming elements keep their original forms and qualities, the other that they completely lose them. This passage presents both views and refutes them using logical and empirical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read and identify the two doctrines
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the two false doctrines and how they are presented.
The first doctrine claims elements retain forms and qualities; the second claims they acquire a single new form.
2
Analyze the refutations
For each doctrine, see how the author refutes it. The first refutation is a claim of certain knowledge; the second has two logical and empirical arguments.
The refutation of the second doctrine uses both logical impossibility and experimental evidence.
3
Reflect on the empirical proof
Notice the mention of evaporation, distillation, and putrefaction as empirical evidence against the second doctrine. This shows the author's use of experimental observation.
The cucurbit and alembic refer to distillation apparatus used in alchemy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ههنا مذاهب أخر فاسدة . الأول: أن العناصر باقية على صورها وصرافة كيفياتها، وإنما تحس بالكيفية المتوسطة لفرط الاختلاط وعدم الامتياز عند الحس. ورد بأن عدم بقاء العناصر على كيفياتها عند تماسها معلوم قطعاً. الثاني : إن امتزاج العناصر وتفاعلها قد أدى بها إلى أن نخلع صورها، ولا يكون لواحد منها صورتها الخاصة، وتلبس حينئذ صورة واحدة، فيصير لها هيولي واحدة، وصورة واحدة، ثم منهم من جعل تلك الصورة أمراً متوسطاً بين الصور المتضادة للبسائط، ومنهم من جعلها صورة أخرى للنوعيات، أي صورة توجد لبعض الأنواع الموجودة في الأعيان . ورد بوجهين : أحدهما أن تفاسد الصور سواء كان على وجه الانكسار أو الزوال بالكلية، إما أن يكون معاً أو على التعاقب وكلاهما فاسد لما مرّ في الكيفيات، ولا يجوز أن يجعل الفاعل ههنا هو الكيفية كالصورة في انكسار الكيفيات، لأن في فساد الصورة فساد آثارها أعني الكيفيات. وثانيهما أنه لو كان كذلك لما اختلفت أجزاء الممتزج بالتبخر والتقاطر والترمد واللازم باطل بحكم القرع والإنبيق.
Then here are other corrupt doctrines. First: that the elements remain in their forms and the purity of their qualities, and that one only perceives the intermediate quality due to extreme mixing and lack of distinction by the senses. It is refuted by saying that the non-persistence of the elements upon their qualities when they come into contact is known with certainty. Second: that the mixing and interaction of the elements has led them to cast off their forms, and none of them has its own form, and then they clothe a single form, so they come to have a single matter and a single form. Then some of them made that form a thing intermediate between the opposing forms of the simples, and some of them made it another form for species, i.e. a form that exists for some of the species existing in substances. It is refuted in two ways: one of them is that the corruption of forms, whether by way of breaking or complete disappearance, either occurs simultaneously or successively, and both are corrupt as was mentioned regarding qualities, and it is not permissible to make the agent here the quality like the form in the breaking of qualities, because in the corruption of form there is the corruption of its effects, i.e. the qualities. And the second is that if it were so, the parts of the mixture would not differ by evaporation, distillation, and putrefaction, and the necessary consequence is false by the rule of the cucurbit and alembic.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage refutes two false theories about what happens when elements mix to form compound substances. The first theory claims that elements retain their original forms and qualities, but due to extreme mixing, the senses perceive an intermediate quality. The author rejects this by stating that it is certain knowledge that elements do not keep their qualities when mixing. The second theory proposes that elements completely abandon their forms and take on a single new form, resulting in one matter and one form. Some say this new form is intermediate, others that it is a species form. The author offers two refutations: first, if forms corrupt either simultaneously or successively, both are impossible for reasons already discussed in the section on qualities, and the agent of corruption cannot be a quality because the corruption of a form entails corruption of its effects (the qualities). Second, if the theory were true, the parts of a mixture would not differ through processes like evaporation, distillation, and putrefaction, but they do, so the theory is false. The passage concludes by invoking experimental evidence from alchemy (cucurbit and alembic).

صور
كيفيات
امتزاج

تفاسد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: In mixture, elements either retain their qualities or completely lose their forms.
Correction: The author argues that elements neither persist unchanged nor vanish entirely; they undergo a genuine transformation that is proven by logical and empirical evidence.

Checkpoint

D) It leads to an infinite regress of forms.

Key Takeaway
Elements in a mixture undergo a real transformation that is neither complete retention nor total annihilation, as proven by logical reasoning and experimental chemistry.
